<span id="freeTextContainer12259050645363185855">The Dursleys were so mean and hideous that summer that all Harry Potter wanted was to get back to the Hogwarts School for Witchcraft and Wizardry. But just as he's packing his bags, Harry receives a warning from a strange, impish creature named Dobby who says that if Harry Potter returns to Hogwarts, disaster will strike.<br /><br />And strike it does. For in Harry's second year at Ho</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12259050645363185855">The Dursleys were so mean and hideous that summer that all Harry Potter wanted was to get back to the Hogwarts School for Witchcraft and Wizardry. But just as he's packing his bags, Harry receives a warning from a strange, impish creature named Dobby who says that if Harry Potter returns to Hogwarts, disaster will strike.<br /><br />And strike it does. For in Harry's second year at Hogwarts, fresh torments and horrors arise, including an outrageously stuck-up new professor, Gilderoy Lockheart, a spirit named Moaning Myrtle who haunts the girls' bathroom, and the unwanted attentions of Ron Weasley's younger sister, Ginny.<br /><br />But each of these seem minor annoyances when the real trouble begins, and someone—or something—starts turning Hogwarts students to stone. Could it be Draco Malfoy, a more poisonous rival than ever? Could it possibly be Hagrid, whose mysterious past is finally told? Or could it be the one everyone at Hogwarts most suspects…Harry Potter himself.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12259050645363185855">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1360691715">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2391843404050144372">JK Rowling really knows how to write a great book, thats for sure! Although this wasn't my favorite book in the series, it definitely wasn't because it was bad. I loved the plot and conflict, even though it wasn't as intense as the others were. I was definitely shocked at the end...so epic and mind blowing!</span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/224912.Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Paperback 9780747538486" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3452652-raeleen-lemay?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer108852940">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9230223245500471951"><em>Re-Read in December 2015 for Harry Christmas to You</em><br /><br />This time around I realized how much more entertaining this book is compared to the movie. Nothing against the movie because I LOVE it, but this book has so many more fun scenes! Like Arthur and Lucius PHYSICALLY FIGHTING EACH OTHER and Dobby tossing Lucius down a flight of stairs at the end. Reading this aloud with Kyle literally had us laughing like crazy. I love this series so much oh my Rowling.<br /><br /><em>Re-Read in December 2014 for Harry Christmas to</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9230223245500471951"><em>Re-Read in December 2015 for Harry Christmas to You</em><br /><br />This time around I realized how much more entertaining this book is compared to the movie. Nothing against the movie because I LOVE it, but this book has so many more fun scenes! Like Arthur and Lucius PHYSICALLY FIGHTING EACH OTHER and Dobby tossing Lucius down a flight of stairs at the end. Reading this aloud with Kyle literally had us laughing like crazy. I love this series so much oh my Rowling.<br /><br /><em>Re-Read in December 2014 for Harry Christmas to You</em><br /><br />OH MY LORD VOLDEMORT.<br /><br />In this book we get more little hints to events to come in future books (Horcrux stuff, a mention of Voldemort having left a part of himself/his powers in Harry, etc.) WHICH WAS AWESOME. I find that every time I read these books I notice more things, which was definitely true this time around. <br /><br />One thing I did notice, which COULD HAVE SOLVED EVERYTHING:<br /><br />At the beginning of the book when they're leaving for King's Cross, Ginny forgets her diary and has to back for it. SHE NEARLY LEFT IT BEHIND. OH MAN. <br /><br />Overall, this was a great time, but I'm excited to finally get to my favorite books in the series!!!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_173434838">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173434838" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4632071-lora" class="left imgcol" title="Lora"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1305237530p2/4632071.jpg" alt="Lora" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/173434838?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 13, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4632071-lora" class="user" title="Lora">Lora</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15881.Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Hardcover 9780439064866" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of the first</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lora by: </span>
      my enjoyment of the first
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=lib-read" class="actionLinkLite">lib-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=middle-grade-lit" class="actionLinkLite">middle-grade-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer173434838">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6367329206349664007"><strong><em>"It is our choices, Harry, that show what we truly are, far more than our abilities."</em> - Albus Dumbledore</strong><br /><br />Such a wise wizard.<br /><br />You know how sometimes when you read the first in a series and it turns out so much better than you originally anticipated, it makes you a little apprehensive when starting the sequel? Well, I felt that way before starting this, but I can definitely say that <em>Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</em> is another fabulous installment in the rightfully beloved Harry Potter series!</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6367329206349664007"><strong><em>"It is our choices, Harry, that show what we truly are, far more than our abilities."</em> - Albus Dumbledore</strong><br /><br />Such a wise wizard.<br /><br />You know how sometimes when you read the first in a series and it turns out so much better than you originally anticipated, it makes you a little apprehensive when starting the sequel? Well, I felt that way before starting this, but I can definitely say that <em>Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</em> is another fabulous installment in the rightfully beloved Harry Potter series!<br />And while I <em>will</em> admit to not loving it quite as much as its predecessor, I still enjoyed it a great deal. <br />I think the reason for my not liking it as much can be mostly credited to the introduction of a new character, Professor Lockhart. Lockhart is an annoyingly pretentious wizard who is completely full of himself, and the majority of his teachings were based on his own life and his supposed brushes with death that he escaped only because of his "heroism" and great knowledge of the magic arts. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Riiiiiiiiight. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />In a summary, I didn't find the story involving Lockhart quite as interesting as Harry's realization of his true abilities and the escapades of his first year at Hogwarts.<br /><br />But HP II undoubtedly still has plenty of hilarious moments and magical wonders - not to mention the lovely cast of characters - to more than compensate for this particular installment's slightly lacking plot. Hence the five stars. :)<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[<img class="escapedImg" src="http://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/photos/1308084012p8/284271.jpg" /><br /><br />Very clever Ms. Rowling, very clever indeed. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />FAVORITE QUOTE: <em>"I've heard you hate those Muggles you live with," said Ernie swiftly.<br />"It's not possible to live with the Dursleys and not hate them," said Harry. "I'd like to see you try it."</em><br /><br />Next up is <a title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (Harry Potter, #3) by J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban__Harry_Potter___3_">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a>, and I'm very much looking forward to it.<br /><br />**********************************************************<br /><br /><strong>My reviews of other titles in this series:</strong><br /><br /><a href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173429036">Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone</a><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6367329206349664007">...more</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer981371719">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer301534090006402693">Overall, I loved this, and I can't wait to start <a title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (Harry Potter, #3) by J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban__Harry_Potter___3_">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a> today. <br /><br />Quick thoughts on the things that stood out to me: <br /><br />Wow, the Dursleys were even more loathsome in this book than the first. <br />I love the Weasleys even more than I already did.<br />I am so glad my mother never sent me a Howler.<br />I thought Dobby was annoying in the movie (which I saw when it came out over a decade ago, not having read the book) but I thought he was awesome in the book. In fact, we rewatched the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText301534090006402693">Overall, I loved this, and I can't wait to start <a title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (Harry Potter, #3) by J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5.Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban__Harry_Potter___3_">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</a> today. <br /><br />Quick thoughts on the things that stood out to me: <br /><br />Wow, the Dursleys were even more loathsome in this book than the first. <br />I love the Weasleys even more than I already did.<br />I am so glad my mother never sent me a Howler.<br />I thought Dobby was annoying in the movie (which I saw when it came out over a decade ago, not having read the book) but I thought he was awesome in the book. In fact, we rewatched the movie last night, and not only was it as unsatisfying as I remember it, it's just a shit adaptation of this book.<br />I thought it was delightful that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[the flying car went into the Forbidden Forest and went feral <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br />Tom Riddle's diary was really, really awesome. The entire idea and execution were fantastic.<br /><br />I loved it when Dumbledore told Harry, "It is our choices, Harry, that show what we truly are, far more than our abilities." I hope that, as the series goes on, we have more scenes with him, because I really love his wisdom.<br /><br />My minor complaints seem a little nitpicky, and I suppose that if I'm going to suspend disbelief to accept that wizards are real, I should be able to accept that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[none of the adults at Hogwarts would look in Hermione's fist to see the paper that Harry and Ron found after she was Petrified <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Fawkes somehow just found his way into the Chamber of Secrets <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but I'm an adult and if I'd read this as a kid I wouldn't have cared for a single moment.<br /><br /><br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_14146681">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14146681" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/858949-chris" class="left imgcol" title="Chris"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1208350750p2/858949.jpg" alt="Chris" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/14146681?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 09, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/858949-chris" class="user" title="Chris">Chris</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/858949-chris?shelf=harry-potter" class="actionLinkLite">harry-potter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14146681">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1804409639831201585"><em>Since pretty much everyone I know has read these books, I figure reviewing them is pretty pointless. But with the new book coming out in a couple of weeks, I have to go through them beginning to end. To make the reviews more entertaining, I will be doing them in a variety of unexpected formats. For this review, I will be writing as someone who's just getting into Freudian theory.</em><br /><br />From the very beginning, the true nature of this story is quite obvious - The Chamber of Secrets. There is only one "c</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1804409639831201585"><em>Since pretty much everyone I know has read these books, I figure reviewing them is pretty pointless. But with the new book coming out in a couple of weeks, I have to go through them beginning to end. To make the reviews more entertaining, I will be doing them in a variety of unexpected formats. For this review, I will be writing as someone who's just getting into Freudian theory.</em><br /><br />From the very beginning, the true nature of this story is quite obvious - The Chamber of Secrets. There is only one "chamber of secrets" that is of any human concern, and it is no coincidence that the book of such a title was written by a woman.<br /><br />By sending her young, immature male character, Harry (whose name, along with Tom and Dick, just happens to be one of the "universal" male names) into the mysterious Chamber, Rowling is exploring her memories of early childhood sexuality. The Chamber is filled not only with mystery, but danger and legend - its very existence is debated, which no doubt refers to the elusive female orgasm.<br /><br />Ms. Rowling, whose sexual impulses have no doubt been unfulfilled over the years, is attempting to fulfill them by way of her own fiction. She has created a perfect sexual explorer in Harry Potter - a young, innocent and noble young man whose powers have not yet matured. Obviously a male that Rowling would feel comfortable with. This is especially interesting given the actual resident of the Chamber of Secrets - a huge, deadly serpent. And there's only one thing that a huge, terrible serpent can represent.<br /><br />Rowling's sexual past is the fertile ground in which this book was grown. It is her cathartic attempt to win over the guilty feelings that she's repressed from her former sexual life, the one she regrets more than anything else, by manufacturing a hero. That hero, in Harry Potter, represents the type of man for whom she would "open" her "chamber - pure of heart and noble of intention and, most importantly, under her control. The vanquishing of the serpent-symbol is her victory, leaving her free to explore other aspects of her life, including the eventual resolution of the Electra complex that appears to have been built up around Professor Dumbledore...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1804409639831201585">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1268939794">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10422201809208667396"><br />I have been so far behind in my reading and reviews...dealing with...life. I spent the whole month (so far) of August trying to play catch up. And now that I have sort of done that- I left this one review till the end...because even though the last thing that my lovely <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241902773">Stepheny aka Ms. Thaaaaaaaaaaang</a> would want for me is to feel pressure- I do...OH, I really do. I feel the pressure to put out the best review that I can possibly think of right now...just for her- for her favorite series. The ser</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10422201809208667396"><br />I have been so far behind in my reading and reviews...dealing with...life. I spent the whole month (so far) of August trying to play catch up. And now that I have sort of done that- I left this one review till the end...because even though the last thing that my lovely <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241902773">Stepheny aka Ms. Thaaaaaaaaaaang</a> would want for me is to feel pressure- I do...OH, I really do. I feel the pressure to put out the best review that I can possibly think of right now...just for her- for her favorite series. The series that got her through the hard times in her life. Books she thinks of as family.<br /><br />I'm not worthy. But I am going to try...<br /><br /><strong>Gryffindor</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo a38e481d-8e2e-4c4d-8b48-d0227584f7df_zpsqrtcdlv5.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440357315i/15965673.jpg" />- Passionate about their beliefs, and standing up for what they believe in. First to defend their friends. They prefer to deal with a situation directly, even if it means a fight - and they want that fight to be a fair one.<br /><br /><strong>Ravenclaw</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo a614d302-a785-494d-b940-8800311f371b_zpsdcynvsmc.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440357315i/15965674.jpg" />- Defined by curiosity and the love of learning- first and foremost. A Ravenclaw will always seek knowledge. They want to know the why of everything. They love learning, and will want to seek as much knowledge as possible.<br /><br /><strong>Hufflepuff</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 5845737c-6412-4756-8408-3cdedb77714c_zpskkqphwrq.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440357315i/15965675.jpg" />- Ultimately, Hufflepuffs are interested in helping both people and animals- much less confrontational or daring than the other houses. They are also the least likely to care about individual achievement or House points- more apt to to focus on their relationships to others rather than things they personally have done.<br /><br /><strong>Slytherin</strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 72f77aaf-493b-4b62-a1fb-1e2734aec1c9_zpskizu9asm.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440357315i/15965676.jpg" />- Slytherins are seeking individual greatness, and the dark and mysterious appeals to them greatly, even if it seems dangerous. They’ll go for experiences that other houses are too afraid to touch.<br /><br />Which house are you?<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.allthetests.com/quiz30/quiz/1345079778/Gryffindor-Hufflepuff-Ravenclaw-or-Slytherin" target="_blank">http://www.allthetests.com/quiz30/qui...</a><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo d5c08b43-47df-4622-b663-3352bb06425c_zpsh3oonj5c.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440359347i/15965792.jpg" /><br /><br />Harry has spent another horrible summer dealing with the Dursleys...but hope comes with a rescue from one of his best friends- Ron Weeeeeeeeeasley *said with a squeaky British accent*- and his father's flying car.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 11ffe7a6-62f8-43b6-be9b-1dc527f93436_zpsrg577ixt.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440357315i/15965678.jpg" /><br /><br />So in the dead of night- they arrive at Hogwarts- ready for what the year ahead awaits them...<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" /><img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo 77019b8a-da3a-411a-89bb-9d29efc2a86b_zpsleubssp4.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440357504i/15965683.jpg" /><br /><br />As usual I will not give too much away...but excitement lurks behind these pages- for young and old....and I for one (somewhere in the middle)- am looking forward to what comes next.<br /><br />* Even though I like for people to think I fall under the mysterious Slytherin- No matter how much I try- I am still a Hufflepuff at heart...apparently.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_83629671">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83629671" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3112505-elisa" class="left imgcol" title="Elisa "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452314605p2/3112505.jpg" alt="Elisa " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/83629671?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 15, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3112505-elisa" class="user" title="Elisa ">Elisa </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15881.Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Hardcover 9780439064866" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3112505-elisa?shelf=kids-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">kids-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3112505-elisa?shelf=seven-greatest-books-ever" class="actionLinkLite">seven-greatest-books-ever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer83629671">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11274571137081154796">A lot of people cite this book as their least favorite in the Potter saga; many of my friends included. When I asked one of my friends why he felt it was the worst of the bunch, he gave me a very reasonable reply. He'd come in late on the Potter game, having only read them last year in fact, when a Professor of his was walking them through what it takes to be a good mystery-- using <a title="Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone (Harry Potter, #1) by J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3.Harry_Potter_and_the_Sorcerer_s_Stone__Harry_Potter___1_">Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone</a> as an example of a perfectly fashioned mystery.<br /><br />Moving on to the second book,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11274571137081154796">A lot of people cite this book as their least favorite in the Potter saga; many of my friends included. When I asked one of my friends why he felt it was the worst of the bunch, he gave me a very reasonable reply. He'd come in late on the Potter game, having only read them last year in fact, when a Professor of his was walking them through what it takes to be a good mystery-- using <a title="Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone (Harry Potter, #1) by J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3.Harry_Potter_and_the_Sorcerer_s_Stone__Harry_Potter___1_">Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone</a> as an example of a perfectly fashioned mystery.<br /><br />Moving on to the second book, <a title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets (Harry Potter, #2) by J.K. Rowling" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15881.Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets__Harry_Potter___2_">Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</a>, my friend (let's call him Rex) found that this book wasn't up to standard mystery-wise in the way the first book had been, which is what he'd been expecting. Maybe it's because I first read it as a child, or it's maybe because I was more interested in the fantasy aspect, but I never really cared, nor do I care now that it doesn't follow the same standard mystery guidelines. <br /><br />Rex was the only person who gave me an answer other than "I don't know, I just don't like it as much," so therefore his is the only one that I'm able to analyze. But enough negativity, allow me to explain what I <em>do</em> like about it.<br /><br />Um, Ron's broken wand? Hysterical. Well, if I'm being honest, any single scene including Mr. Ron Weasley is bound to make me smile and any interaction between him and Hermione (yes, even this early on) is bound to make me squee!!!!!!!!!! Notice how quick he is to jump to Hermione's defense; notice how distraught he is over Hermione's being petrified. Oh, how I love them.<br /><br />To add a few more- Harry's first trip to the Burrow! The flying car! Fred and George marching ahead of Harry, announcing him mockingly as the Heir of Slytherin! The singing Valentine's Day Dwarves! And our introduction to the Whomping Willow! Come on people, this is classic stuff!<br /><br />I also love the part Ginny Weasley plays in this book; not so much the whole "helping the Heir of Slytherin thing," but her mad crush on Harry. Maybe because I was granted the fortune/misfortune of having a brother a grade above me, I also had the wonderful fortune/misfortune of crushing on all his super hott (yes with two t's) friends. Ah, how I remember the days of pining for them, of whining over their lack of return interest, of cursing my blasted gapped teeth and frizzy hair. Of course, unlike Ginny I was never able to woo any of them in the end, (even after my braces!) but I still think I did alright as far as men go;)<br /><br />Okay, back to the text. I even enjoy ol' Lockhart, for what he's worth. Yeah, he's obnoxious, but that's the point, right? And yeah, the degree to whch he is obnoxious is a little cartoony and unrealistic, but let's not forget- this is a children's book, after all. <br /><br />Chamber of Secrets also sees Harry destroying his first Horcrux, and offers us our first insight into one Tom Riddle. I would never discount this book, or cast it so carelessly aside as least favorite of the bunch (I don't believe in ranking these books, by the way). Anyway, it receives a full five stars from me with zero hesitation. I appreciate it's contribution to the Potter world and will look forward to reading it again when the time comes...which it will.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11274571137081154796">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/6278820-inge" class="user" title="Inge">Inge</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer207710904">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12676868066412715953">The Harry Potter series is like one giant puzzle, and during every book, tiny puzzle pieces start fitting together and forming a whole. There are hints everywhere about what's going to happen, sort of like inside jokes for people who've already read the books, but the mystery remains. J.K. Rowling keeps you guessing up until the final pages.<br /><br />I love how every character brings something else to the table. Ron's dry comments, Fred and George's pranks, Hermione's cleverness, Dumbledore's charming str</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12676868066412715953">The Harry Potter series is like one giant puzzle, and during every book, tiny puzzle pieces start fitting together and forming a whole. There are hints everywhere about what's going to happen, sort of like inside jokes for people who've already read the books, but the mystery remains. J.K. Rowling keeps you guessing up until the final pages.<br /><br />I love how every character brings something else to the table. Ron's dry comments, Fred and George's pranks, Hermione's cleverness, Dumbledore's charming strangeness. Even side characters like Mr and Mrs Weasley have such a strong individuality. They're all fleshed out.<br /><br /><em>Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</em> is an exciting, thrilling read. It makes you think along with the Golden Trio and laugh out loud. It makes you cheer characters on and boo others. You're engaged for the entire story and there's no way out. You can't escape. Hogwarts is your home.<br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2rd9mow">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380358778ra/709934.gif" /></a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12676868066412715953">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_241902773">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241902773" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny" class="left imgcol" title="Stepheny"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446648446p2/7091879.jpg" alt="Stepheny" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/241902773?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 24, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny" class="user" title="Stepheny">Stepheny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/13603662-harry-potter-and-the-chamber-of-secrets" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=books-everyone-should-read" class="actionLinkLite">books-everyone-should-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=favorite-series" class="actionLinkLite">favorite-series</a>,

              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=hands-down-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">hands-down-favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=coming-of-age" class="actionLinkLite">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=like-a-meth-addiction" class="actionLinkLite">like-a-meth-addiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=badd-ass-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">badd-ass-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=guilty-pleasure-reads" class="actionLinkLite">guilty-pleasure-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=reliving-my-childhood" class="actionLinkLite">reliving-my-childhood</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer241902773">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2121914894258310984"><br />About a year ago I <s>threw a tantrum</s> begged Delee to read Harry Potter with me. She had never read it and I just simply can’t accept that. Because let’s face it:<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433273395i/15075416._SX540_.jpg" />.<br /><br />Well, she inevitably, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900860104"> jumped on the bandwagon</a> with the rest of the world. I was so thrilled that she not only finally read it but that she loved it. It took her a whole year to get around to the next book, but she did and that’s all that matters. She’s already given this one <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1268939794?book_show_action=false"> 5 stars</a>! AND we’ve scheduled our reading of Prisoner of Azkaba</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2121914894258310984"><br />About a year ago I <s>threw a tantrum</s> begged Delee to read Harry Potter with me. She had never read it and I just simply can’t accept that. Because let’s face it:<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433273395i/15075416._SX540_.jpg" />.<br /><br />Well, she inevitably, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/900860104"> jumped on the bandwagon</a> with the rest of the world. I was so thrilled that she not only finally read it but that she loved it. It took her a whole year to get around to the next book, but she did and that’s all that matters. She’s already given this one <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1268939794?book_show_action=false"> 5 stars</a>! AND we’ve scheduled our reading of Prisoner of Azkaban for August** of this year. I’m one excited Potthead!<br /><br />Chamber of Secrets catches some heat from fans for being too much like the first one. But, I assure you it’s really not <em>that</em> similar. Sure, there’s our favorite trio once again keeping secrets from adults who could totally use that information. Sure, there’s something sinister going on in the school causing everyone’s feathers to be ruffled. Sure, there’s a Professor who isn’t exactly who he says he is.<br /><br />But, this story is different. And damn it, it is FUN. I can’t tell you, now, how many times I have reread this series. What I <strong>can </strong> tell you is that every single time this one gets funnier and funnier. There was more than one occasion where my giggling fits caused the bed to shake leading to Jerrid’s disgruntled complaints. His grumblings went unnoticed though, for how am I to show any self-control whenever Professor Lockhart is in the room? <br /><br />JK Rowling’s books are something truly special, something that will live within us for the rest of our lives. The quotes from these books are as engrained in our brains as our own names. I look forward to continuing this journey with Delee. I can only hope that there will be others that will follow her lead and give these books a chance when they thought them not worth their time. Trust me on this, if you’re not reading these books you’re making a huge mistake. <br /><br />Just remember what Dumbledore says:<br /><strong> “It is our choices, Harry, that show what we truly are, far more than our abilities.” </strong><br /><br />You’re my next <s>victim</s> prospect, Jeff. Best be ready, MahFah.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2121914894258310984">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer401779868868045352"><strong>Rating: 5/5 stars</strong><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1292445284?type=review#rating_59695056">Click here</a> to read my review of Harry Potter and the Sorcerers Stone.<br /><br /><em>Ron breaks his wand,<br /><br /><img width="350" height="146" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449785801ra/17337183.gif" /><br /><br />now Ginny's gone,<br /><br /><img width="350" height="147" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449785801ra/17337184.gif" /><br /><br />and Harry's in mortal danger.<br /><br /><img width="350" height="148" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449785801ra/17337185.gif" /><br /><br />Tom Riddle hides his snake inside<br /><br /><img width="350" height="146" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449785801ra/17337186.gif" /><br /><br />his ginormous secret chamber.</em><br /><br /><img width="350" height="145" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449785801i/17337187._SX540_.png" /><br /><br />(From <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y57sYHIDP_Y">Harry Potter in 99 seconds</a>, which BTW is super awesome!)<br /><br />I think this goes for a lot of people, but the Chamber of Secrets is my least favorite Harry Potter book (or rather I like the other ones more). But I still enjoyed the hell out of it, and it still deserves 5 stars.<br /><br /><br /><br /><u> <strong>Things t</strong></u></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText401779868868045352"><strong>Rating: 5/5 stars</strong><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1292445284?type=review#rating_59695056">Click here</a> to read my review of Harry Potter and the Sorcerers Stone.<br /><br /><em>Ron breaks his wand,<br /><br /><img width="350" height="146" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449785801ra/17337183.gif" /><br /><br />now Ginny's gone,<br /><br /><img width="350" height="147" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449785801ra/17337184.gif" /><br /><br />and Harry's in mortal danger.<br /><br /><img width="350" height="148" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449785801ra/17337185.gif" /><br /><br />Tom Riddle hides his snake inside<br /><br /><img width="350" height="146" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449785801ra/17337186.gif" /><br /><br />his ginormous secret chamber.</em><br /><br /><img width="350" height="145" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449785801i/17337187._SX540_.png" /><br /><br />(From <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y57sYHIDP_Y">Harry Potter in 99 seconds</a>, which BTW is super awesome!)<br /><br />I think this goes for a lot of people, but the Chamber of Secrets is my least favorite Harry Potter book (or rather I like the other ones more). <div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_4148875">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4148875" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/114559-namratha" class="left imgcol" title="Namratha"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1406702134p2/114559.jpg" alt="Namratha" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/4148875?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 12, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/114559-namratha" class="user" title="Namratha">Namratha</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/480478.Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Paperback 9781551922447" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=journey-within" class="actionLinkLite">journey-within</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=adventure" class="actionLinkLite">adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=mythology" class="actionLinkLite">mythology</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=childrens-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">childrens-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=ya-lit" class="actionLinkLite">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=tween-time" class="actionLinkLite">tween-time</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=books-i-love" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-love</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=pottermania" class="actionLinkLite">pottermania</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=epic-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=children-s" class="actionLinkLite">children-s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4148875">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17727580235898660616">In a bid to recapture the Harry Potteresque brand of nostalgia, I am re-reading the series. And loving every bit of it. <br /><br />I always find that the second offering in a long-running series is always the most fulfilling. After the first book, we have the character profiles down to a tee, we have decided on our personal favourites and pet-peeves and we can easily summon up the scenery and the ambience. So now it’s just a question of belting-up and getting ready for more nail-biting action.<br />And <strong> <u>Harry Po</u></strong></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17727580235898660616">In a bid to recapture the Harry Potteresque brand of nostalgia, I am re-reading the series. And loving every bit of it. <br /><br />I always find that the second offering in a long-running series is always the most fulfilling. After the first book, we have the character profiles down to a tee, we have decided on our personal favourites and pet-peeves and we can easily summon up the scenery and the ambience. So now it’s just a question of belting-up and getting ready for more nail-biting action.<br />And <strong>
  <u>Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</u>
</strong> does just that. <br /><br /><strong>Harry</strong> knows who’s baying for his blood (<em><strong>Malfoy</strong>, <strong>Snape</strong> and good ol’Mouldy-<strong>Voldy</strong></em>) He has a clearer picture of his own powers and abilities. I won’t mention the plot as most of us already know it by rote and those who don’t, are getting converted...as I speak.<br /><br />The high point of the second book is a mysterious...erm....MYSTERY. Rather than laboring on about Harry’s traumatized past and his future trials, it deals with his actual adventures in the present day. Mysterious mumblings in the walls, an unknown beast lurking in some obscure chamber and hapless victims, this book has all the makings of a classic detective novel. Harry Potter gets a chance to prove that all the adulation and hero-worship is justified and he puts up a knock-‘em dead, magnificent fight. <strong>Rowling</strong> manages to weave in her wise homilies towards the end <blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>(“It is our choices, Harry, that show us what we truly are, far more than our abilities.” )</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote> and yet again, it fits perfectly. Not preachy, not patronizing but tailor-made to clear Harry’s misgivings.<br /><br />A rich, satisfying read.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17727580235898660616">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/624327642?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 10, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19590155-vane-j" class="user" title="Vane J.">Vane J.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15881.Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Hardcover 9780439064866" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=amazing-characters" class="actionLinkLite">amazing-characters</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=2012" class="actionLinkLite">2012</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=speshul-snowflake" class="actionLinkLite">speshul-snowflake</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=all-the-feels" class="actionLinkLite">all-the-feels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer624327642">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12636281501481095119">I am one of those people who grew up with the Harry Potter movies rather than with the books (I'm not ashamed to admit, either, that I loved the movies and still do, despite them missing some of the awesomeness), and I was one of those who refused to read the books because I didn't want to be part of the hype and it actually made me sick. Gratefully, 4 years ago I decided to give in. The big surprise was that I ended up loving the series, the story but most of all, its characters.<br /><br />That said, I mu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12636281501481095119">I am one of those people who grew up with the Harry Potter movies rather than with the books (I'm not ashamed to admit, either, that I loved the movies and still do, despite them missing some of the awesomeness), and I was one of those who refused to read the books because I didn't want to be part of the hype and it actually made me sick. Gratefully, 4 years ago I decided to give in. The big surprise was that I ended up loving the series, the story but most of all, its characters.<br /><br />That said, I must continue. This second installment is not the best of them, yet it's still very good. The mystery was not so easy to guess, and god, the characters! I love them all! Except, of course, 2 of them.<br /><br /><strong>#1: Mr. Gilderoy Lockhart.</strong> Because I am not fond of bad teachers. I seriously abhor them. I wanted this fraud of a man dead ever since he appeared for the first time. The worst part is that he taught what probably was the most important class of them all.<br /><br /><strong>#2: Dobby.</strong> Even though I grew fond of him later, you have to admit he was very annoying t the beginning. And please someone tell me I'm not the only one who doesn't fall for his almost-killed-Harry-but-did-it-with-good-intentions-so-I-will-punish-myself-for-it bullshit.<br /><br />Originally, my rating was 4 stars, but then I decided I should round it to 5 because I really truly love this. I think I miss the characters' innocence already and want to dive in again, but I will hold myself from doing so. Now off to re-read book 3!</span>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_4273354">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4273354" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/251287-swaps55" class="left imgcol" title="Swaps55"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1376517361p2/251287.jpg" alt="Swaps55" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/4273354?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 16, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/251287-swaps55" class="user" title="Swaps55">Swaps55</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15881.Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Hardcover 9780439064866" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/251287-swaps55?shelf=scifi-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">scifi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/251287-swaps55?shelf=harry-potter" class="actionLinkLite">harry-potter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4273354">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7569120815285177458">While the story fits neatly together and again, her imagination is fantastic, the flat characters that play to extreme stereotypes take a lot of the enjoymeny out of this story. <br /><br />There is no excuse for Gilderoy Lockhart. Granted, his fame obsession and ludicrous self-absorption make for some amusing Rowling-esque moments that make the series good (such as a dozen Lockharts running for cover in the photo frames with rollers in their hair), but at the expense of the reader's patience. This degree o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7569120815285177458">While the story fits neatly together and again, her imagination is fantastic, the flat characters that play to extreme stereotypes take a lot of the enjoymeny out of this story. <br /><br />There is no excuse for Gilderoy Lockhart. Granted, his fame obsession and ludicrous self-absorption make for some amusing Rowling-esque moments that make the series good (such as a dozen Lockharts running for cover in the photo frames with rollers in their hair), but at the expense of the reader's patience. This degree of narcissism, even if plausible in the real world, stretches my suspension of disbelief too far. Like every page with Malfoy on it, I'd rather flip past them than read them. <br /><br />The greatest problem I have with this series is the two dimensional villains (or irritating Defense Against the Dark Arts teachers). Good villains should draw out some sort of sympathy in the reader, or reveal at some point their humanity. At the very least, you should be able to understand why they are the way they are, and that back story allows you to look at them from a different perspective. This moment never happens for Lockhart, and incidentally it never happens for Malfoy. <br /><br />Rowling allowed the perfect opportunity to make Malfoy a good, three dimensional villain when Harry and Ron used the Polyjuice potion. For the first time, we had Malfoy out of the public eye and in private, where we could see the real him, and not the front everyone else sees. Here was the chance to see his humanity – that he’s such a prick because he’s afraid of disappointing his father, that he worries about his grades, that there’s a girl he likes and he’s secretly worried she doesn’t like him back, anything that humanizes him and draws out some sympathy, because thus far he’s gotten nothing more than eye rolls out of me. But we didn’t get that moment. Rowling wrote him no differently than she does when he is on parade in front of everyone, which was really a shame. <br /><br />So, overall, the characters get tiring, but the writing style and imagination are extremely enjoyable. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7569120815285177458">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1469645452">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469645452" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/40792319-councillor" class="left imgcol" title="Councillor"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1437208837p2/40792319.jpg" alt="Councillor" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1469645452?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/40792319-councillor" class="user" title="Councillor">Councillor</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15881.Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Hardcover 9780439064866" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=read-in-german-version" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-german-version</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=20th-century" class="actionLinkLite">20th-century</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=set-in-united-kingdom-ireland" class="actionLinkLite">set-in-united-kingdom-ireland</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=read-2015" class="actionLinkLite">read-2015</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=adventure" class="actionLinkLite">adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=borrowed" class="actionLinkLite">borrowed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=turned-into-film-i-havent-seen-yet" class="actionLinkLite">turned-into-film-i-havent-seen-yet</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/40792319-councillor?shelf=rated-3-and-a-half-stars" class="actionLinkLite">rated-3-and-a-half-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1469645452">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer335837988004662884">How do you review a beloved book which nearly everyone in this world seems to adore and which you wanted to love as well, but ended up being slightly disappointed with? "Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets" is the second book out of the HP series and follows Harry, Ron and Hermione through their adventures during their second year in Hogwarts. After reading (and enjoying) the first book some days ago (and just about ten years too late), my expectations for this second book were probably too</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText335837988004662884">How do you review a beloved book which nearly everyone in this world seems to adore and which you wanted to love as well, but ended up being slightly disappointed with? "Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets" is the second book out of the HP series and follows Harry, Ron and Hermione through their adventures during their second year in Hogwarts. After reading (and enjoying) the first book some days ago (and just about ten years too late), my expectations for this second book were probably too high, as it is often the case with second installments in a series.<br /><br />J.K. Rowling delved deeper into the world of Harry Potter, his friends and his enemies, but in the end, I felt as if we didn't learn many new things about this world. Apart from some very interesting bad-ass moments, the character development lacked some of its profound depth from the first book and ultimately made me consider the book as a transition phase between Harry Potter as a child and a teenager.<br /><br />However, don't you think I didn't enjoy or like it! It was still a great book, a magical world, an exciting plot, but its flaws emerged a little bit more apparently and were unable to fulfil my expectations in their entirety. Draco Malfoy continues to be annoying, not because of the character's annoying appearances, but because of his character traits being nearly non-existing. It can be argued that it is difficult to create full characters out of children, but J.K. Rowling succeeded with trying this procedure with Harry, Ron, Hermione and even Ginny, so why not with Draco? Hopefully, his character is going to be explored in more profundity during the other novels.<br /><br />It seems like I keep defending my relatively low rating of this novel, but Goodreads describes a three-star-rating as 'liked it', and I absolutely did. It simply was no 'really liked it' or 'it was amazing', so I will lower my expectations a little bit and hope to be able to award five stars again after reading the next book.<br /><br /><blockquote>When I'm 80 years old and sitting in my rocking chair, I'll be reading Harry Potter. And my family will say to me, 'After all this time?' And I will say, 'Always.'</blockquote><br />Isn't this a lovely statement? Sources say Alan Rickman created this quote, but others insist on the quote being misattributed, so I'll just leave it at that and turn to the third novel of the Harry Potter series.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="335837988004662884">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_794900310">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/794900310" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/22313662-laz" class="left imgcol" title="Laz"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1445857941p2/22313662.jpg" alt="Laz" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/794900310?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 21, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/22313662-laz" class="user" title="Laz">Laz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7979789-harry-potter-and-the-chamber-of-secrets" title="Paperback 9781408810552" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">magic world lovers</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/22313662-laz?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22313662-laz?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22313662-laz?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22313662-laz?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22313662-laz?shelf=sci-fi" class="actionLinkLite">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/22313662-laz?shelf=all-time-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer794900310">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8646988257698264044"><strong> <blockquote>“It is our choices, Harry, that show what we truly are, far more than our abilities.”</blockquote> </strong><br /><br />While I think the movies are just awesome, I think they fail to capture the magic this book has. This book just enveloped me in my magic. Magic, magic everywhere. Surrounding me. Making me feel like I was a person living inside this magnificent world, but terrifying and dangerous nonetheless.<br /><br />This is the second book in the series and I couldn't have been more satisfied with it, I don't know if there's anything</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8646988257698264044"><strong>
  <blockquote>“It is our choices, Harry, that show what we truly are, far more than our abilities.”</blockquote>
</strong><br /><br />While I think the movies are just awesome, I think they fail to capture the magic this book has. This book just enveloped me in my magic. Magic, magic everywhere. Surrounding me. Making me feel like I was a person living inside this magnificent world, but terrifying and dangerous nonetheless.<br /><br />This is the second book in the series and I couldn't have been more satisfied with it, I don't know if there's anything bad for me to say about it. I don't know why I'd bother myself trying to figure out what are the flaws of the book and I enjoyed myself so much reading it.<br /><br />I'm not one of those people who try to find every needle in a haystack. I can be satisfied with imperfection, and that's not at all imperfect. It met all of my standards I had set after reading the first book. <br /><br />It was adventurous and the world grows more and more complex, just like I wanted it to be. Learning more about magic, was just as wondrous and exciting as it was for Harry, Hermione and Ron and all those other kids at Hogwarts. I almost feel like I'm a student there, which I wish I were. Take out the Basilisk &amp; Voldemort though because I'd shit my pants. Not that the kids weren't afraid. Of course, they were and that makes it that much more real. The kids have a magnet for trouble. <br /><br />It's so deep, it is a book any kid should be reading instead of reading and obsessing about instead of playing pc games all day and night long. I'll be careful enough to teach my kids how to read and appreciate what books give to us. <br /><br />I love that in the end Harry stands alone and face the enemies without the immediate help of Ron &amp; Hermione. They help him along the way, and that's just as important. <br /><br />It was such a great read and writing this after almost 1 year I feel so drawn to just pick up the book and reread it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8646988257698264044">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1221841570">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14117288129392919529">I first realized how much the movies actually sucked after my second reread of this series just last year, I meant to say they <em> lacked in something </em> but that is a mere half-truth. I loved the actors, I do, and the effects of the movies are excellent. I just simply disliked how many, many details were chopped off and I was even turned off by the fact that they did not really follow Rowling's original ideas in some scenes. If you ask me, reading the books is a much better alternative to revisit Ho</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14117288129392919529">I first realized how much the movies actually sucked after my second reread of this series just last year, I meant to say they <em> lacked in something </em> but that is a mere half-truth. I loved the actors, I do, and the effects of the movies are excellent. I just simply disliked how many, many details were chopped off and I was even turned off by the fact that they did not really follow Rowling's original ideas in some scenes. If you ask me, reading the books is a much better alternative to revisit Hogwarts. <br /><br />I stand resolute with my original 5 star rating.<br /><br /><blockquote> <em> "After all this time?"<br /><strong> "Always." </strong> </em> </blockquote><br /><br />I loved the mystery on who's behind the unleashing of the Basilisk. Rowling had kept people guessing and even scattered clues for future cases. <br /><br />When Tom Riddle re-arranged his own name together to form...<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449550074ra/17303683.gif" /><br /><br />I remembered my first expression to be something like this...<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434743710ra/15258258.gif" /><br /><br />It still never failed to surprise me how Rowling may have planned everything right from the beginning itself and I say, <strong> keep them coming. </strong><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449550074ra/17303684.gif" /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iapURD9yBGnFrscCjuLeQlnh8OLXQtW0l1nrtcBloizsfmuXzaAQk0l2s7nwgzjwEBYz+56fkh79UO4nDPBUaQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4qZ1iIfXiL0WcJbClQeCUtuDuxMJPOhxWqXzSADdxNSHckpbdQWcR5qo4nnrZmTgknR4CkDhr9swrPbazEgykQ==')})
  }

              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_121810').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling">About J.K. Rowling</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling"><img alt="1077326" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1415945171p2/1077326.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer828291392834626712">See also: <a title="Robert Galbraith" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith">Robert Galbraith</a><br />Although she writes under the pen name <strong>J.K. Rowling</strong>, pronounced like <em>rolling</em>, her name when her first <em>Harry Potter</em> book was published was simply <strong>Joanne Rowling</strong>. Anticipating that the target audience of young boys might not want to read a book written by a woman, her publishers demanded that she use two initials, rather than her full name. As she had no middle name, she ch</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText828291392834626712">See also: <a title="Robert Galbraith" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith">Robert Galbraith</a><br />Although she writes under the pen name <strong>J.K. Rowling</strong>, pronounced like <em>rolling</em>, her name when her first <em>Harry Potter</em> book was published was simply <strong>Joanne Rowling</strong>. Anticipating that the target audience of young boys might not want to read a book written by a woman, her publishers demanded that she use two initials, rather than her full name. As she had no middle name, she chose <strong>K</strong> as the second initial of her pen name, from her paternal grandmother Kathleen Ada Bulgen Rowling. She calls herself <strong>Jo</strong> and has said, "No one ever called me 'Joanne' when I was young, unless they were angry." Following her marriage, she has sometimes used the name <strong>Joanne Murray</strong> when conducting personal business. During the Leveson Inquiry she gave evidence under the name of <strong>Joanne Kathleen Rowling</strong>. In a 2012 interview, Rowling noted that she no longer cared that people pronounced her name incorrectly.<br /><br />Rowling was born to Peter James Rowling, a Rolls-Royce aircraft engineer, and Anne Rowling (née Volant), on 31 July 1965 in Yate, Gloucestershire, England, 10 miles (16 km) northeast of Bristol. Her mother Anne was half-French and half-Scottish. Her parents first met on a train departing from King's Cross Station bound for Arbroath in 1964. They married on 14 March 1965. Her mother's maternal grandfather, Dugald Campbell, was born in Lamlash on the Isle of Arran. Her mother's paternal grandfather, Louis Volant, was awarded the Croix de Guerre for exceptional bravery in defending the village of Courcelles-le-Comte during the First World War.<br /><br />Rowling's sister Dianne was born at their home when Rowling was 23 months old. The family moved to the nearby village Winterbourne when Rowling was four. She attended St Michael's Primary School, a school founded by abolitionist William Wilberforce and education reformer Hannah More. Her headmaster at St Michael's, Alfred Dunn, has been suggested as the inspiration for the <em>Harry Potter</em> headmaster Albus Dumbledore.<br /><br />As a child, Rowling often wrote fantasy stories, which she would usually then read to her sister. She recalls that: "I can still remember me telling her a story in which she fell down a rabbit hole and was fed strawberries by the rabbit family inside it. Certainly the first story I ever wrote down (when I was five or six) was about a rabbit called Rabbit. He got the measles and was visited by his friends, including a giant bee called Miss Bee." At the age of nine, Rowling moved to Church Cottage in the Gloucestershire village of Tutshill, close to Chepstow, Wales. When she was a young teenager, her great aunt, who Rowling said "taught classics and approved of a thirst for knowledge, even of a questionable kind," gave her a very old copy of Jessica Mitford's autobiography, <em>Hons and Rebels</em>. Mitford became Rowling's heroine, and Rowling subsequently read all of her books.<br /><br />Rowling has said of her teenage years, in an interview with The New Yorker, "I wasn’t particularly happy. I think it’s a dreadful time of life." She had a difficult homelife; her mother was ill and she had a difficult relationship with her father (she is no longer on speaking terms with him). She attended secondary school at Wyedean School and College, where her mother had worked as a technician in the science department. Rowling said of her adolescence, "Hermione [a bookish, know-it-all <em>Harry Potter</em> character] is loosely based on me. She's a caricature of me when I was eleven, which I'm not particularly proud of." Steve Eddy, who taught Rowling English when she first arrived, remembers her as "not exceptional" but "one of a group of girls who were bright, and quite good at English." Sean Harris, her best friend in the Upper Sixth owned a turquoise Ford Anglia, which she says inspired the one in her books.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="828291392834626712">...more</a>

    </div>
